So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** “(constant)\(\cdot P^{1/3}\) + (constant)\(\cdot P\exp(\text{constant}\cdot t)\)” with no extra nonzero terms, and with **no Abs(P)** unless it can be made identical to \(P^{1/3}\) for all real \(P\) (it cannot).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to make it identical to GT for all \(t,P\).

---

### 1.
\(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P e^{c2 t} + c3\sin(\cdots)\).  
Set \(c3=0\). Then choose \(c0=0.4866911314650416\), \(c1=0.4866911314650416\), \(c2=-0.08577402101126279\). Matches GT. ✅

### 2.
\(c0 P e^{c1 t} + c2|P|^{1/3} + c3\sin(\cdots)\).  
Even with \(c3=0\), the term \(|P|^{1/3}\) cannot equal \(P^{1/3}\) for all real \(P\). So cannot match GT as a function of real \(P\). ❌

### 3.
\(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c4 P e^{c5 t} + c6 P\).  
To match GT, must kill polynomial extras: set \(c1=c2=c3=c6=0\). Then pick \(c0\) and \((c4,c5)\) to match coefficients/exponent. Works. ✅

### 4.
Has \(P^3, P^2, P\exp(c4 t), P\), and \(|P|^{1/3}\).  
Even if set \(P^3,P^2,P\) extras to 0, remaining \(|P|^{1/3}\) cannot become \(P^{1/3}\) for all real \(P\). ❌

### 5.
\(c0 P e^{c1 t} + c2 P + c3 P\log(c4|P|+1) + c5|P|^{1/3}\).  
Need \(P^{1/3}\) (not \(|P|^{1/3}\)); also must remove log term and linear \(P\). Cannot produce \(P^{1/3}\) correctly. ❌

### 6.
\(c0 P e^{c1 t} + c3 P^{c2}\log(c4 e^{c5 t}+1) + c6|P|^{1/3}\).  
Cannot turn \(|P|^{1/3}\) into \(P^{1/3}\) for all real \(P\); log term can be zeroed but then still wrong. ❌

### 7.
\(c0 P e^{c1 t} + c2|P|^{1/3} + c3 e^{c4 t}e^{c5|P|}\).  
Cannot get \(P^{1/3}\) (only \(|P|^{1/3}\)); also extra separable exponential in \(|P|\) must be killed. ❌

### 8.
Same issue: \(|P|^{1/3}\) instead of \(P^{1/3}\). ❌

### 9.
\(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 e^{c2 t} + c3 P e^{c4 t}\).  
To match GT, must remove \(P^2 e^{c2 t}\): set \(c1=0\). Then choose \(c0=0.486691...\), \(c3=0.486691...\), \(c4=-0.085774...\). Works. ✅

### 10.
Contains \(P\), \(P^{c1}e^{c3 t}\), \(t e^{c5 t}\), and \(|P|^{c7}\).  
To get \(P^{1/3}\) term would require \(|P|^{c7}\) with \(c7=1/3\), but that’s \(|P|^{1/3}\) not \(P^{1/3}\). Also must kill \(t e^{c5 t}\). No way to get exact GT. ❌

### 11.
\(c1 P^{c0}(c2 t+1)^{c3} + c5 P^{c4} e^{c6 t}\).  
First term is a power of an affine function in \(t\), not an exponential in \(t\), unless \(c3=0\) making it constant in \(t\). Then it can be \( \propto P^{c0}\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c0=1/3\), \(c1=0.486691...\). Second term: set \(c4=1\), \(c5=0.486691...\), \(c6=-0.085774...\). Works. ✅

### 12.

### 13.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: c0*P^(1/3) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)**

where c0 = c2 = 0.4867, c1 = 1/3, c3 = 0.0858.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The GT has exactly two terms: P^(1/3) and P*exp(-αt).

**Key structural requirements:**
- A term proportional to P^(1/3)
- A term proportional to P*exp(negative constant * t)
- No other non-zero terms

Let me go through each candidate, checking if extra terms can be zeroed out and the remaining structure matches.

**Candidate 1:** P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(c6*t)+1)+c7)
Set c3=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 2:** P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*|P|^(1/3) + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1)+c7)
Set c3=0, and since P≥0, |P|^(1/3) = P^(1/3). → P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 3:** P^(1/3)*c0 + P^3*c1 + P^2*c2 + P^2*c3 + P*c4*exp(c5*t) + P*c6
Set c1=0, c2=0, c3=0, c6=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c4*exp(c5*t). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 4:** P^3*c0 + P^2*c1 + P^2*c2 + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5 + c6*|P|^(1/3)

**Candidate 5:** P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P*c3*log(c4*|P|+1) + c5*|P|^(1/3)
Set c2=0, c3=0 → P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c5*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 6:** P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P^c2*c3*log(c4*exp(c5*t)+1) + c6*|P|^(1/3)
Can we zero the middle term? Set c3=0 → P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c6*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 7:** P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*|P|^(1/3) + c3*exp(c4*t)*exp(c5*|P|)
Set c3=0 → P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

Set c3=0 → P*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 10:** P*c0 + P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*t*exp(c5*t) + c6*|P|^c7
Set c0=0, c4=0, c6=0 → P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t). This only gives one term, not two. 
Alternatively, set c4=0, and try to get P^(1/3) from |P|^c7 with c7=1/3, and P*exp(-αt) from P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) with c1=1, plus set c0=0. → P*c2*exp(c3*t) + c6*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH

**Candidate 11:** P^c0*c1*(c2*t+1)^c3 + P^c4*c5*exp(c6*t)

**Candidate 40:** P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*Max(0,c3+t)) + P*c4 + c5*t*exp(c6*t) + c7*|P|^c8

If c3 is very negative, this could be 0 for all relevant t, making the term constant. But we need P*exp(-αt). If t≥0 and c3≥0, then Max(0,c3+t) = c3+t, so P*c1*exp(c2*(c3+t)) = P*c1*exp(c2*c3)*exp(c2*t), which is P*A*exp(c2*t). Set c0=0, c4=0, c5=0 → P*A*exp(c2*t) + c7*P^(1/3). ✓ MATCH (with c3≥0 so Max is always c3+t for t≥0)

Wait, but the Max function makes this conditional. If c3 is large enough that c3+t > 0 for all t in domain (t≥0, so c3≥0 suffices), then Max(0, c3+t) = c3+t. This works. ✓ MATCH
